     <p>
      <b>
       Harley Quinn
      </b>
      (
      <b>
       Dr. Harleen Frances Quinzel
      </b>
      ) is a fictional
      <a href="/wiki/Supervillain" title="Supervillain">
       supervillain
      </a>
      appearing in
      <a href="/wiki/American_comic_book" title="American comic book">
       American comic books
      </a>
      published by
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC Comics
      </a>
      , commonly as an adversary of
      <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">
       Batman
      </a>
      . The character was created by
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dini" title="Paul Dini">
       Paul Dini
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Timm" title="Bruce Timm">
       Bruce Timm
      </a>
      , and first appeared on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_The_Animated_Series" title="Batman: The Animated Series">
        Batman: The Animated Series
       </a>
      </i>
      in September 1992. She later appeared in
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC Comics
      </a>
      '
      <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">
       Batman
      </a>
      comic books, with her first comic book appearance in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Batman_Adventures" title="The Batman Adventures">
        The Batman Adventures
       </a>
      </i>
      #12 (Sept. 1993). Throughout her animated depictions, she is shown to speak with a pronounced
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_English" title="New York City English">
       New York accent
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The character is a frequent accomplice and girlfriend of the
      <a href="/wiki/Joker_(comics)" title="Joker (comics)">
       Joker
      </a>
      , and a girlfriend of the supervillain
      <a href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy_(comics)" title="Poison Ivy (comics)">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      , from whom she gained an immunity to poisons and toxins. Harley Quinn's origin story relates that she met the Joker while working as a
      <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">
       psychiatrist
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Arkham_Asylum" title="Arkham Asylum">
       Arkham Asylum
      </a>
      , where the Joker was a patient. Her name is a play on the name "
      <a href="/wiki/Harlequin" title="Harlequin">
       Harlequin
      </a>
      ," a character which originated in the
      <a href="/wiki/Commedia_dell%27arte" title="Commedia dell'arte">
       commedia dell'arte
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn was originally voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Arleen_Sorkin" title="Arleen Sorkin">
       Arleen Sorkin
      </a>
      in various tie-ins to the
      <a href="/wiki/DC_animated_universe" title="DC animated universe">
       DC animated universe
      </a>
      , and has also been voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Hynden_Walch" title="Hynden Walch">
       Hynden Walch
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tara_Strong" title="Tara Strong">
       Tara Strong
      </a>
      in either
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DC_Animated_Showcase" title="DC Animated Showcase">
       DC Animated Showcases
      </a>
      or in various
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Batman_video_games" title="List of Batman video games">
       video games
      </a>
      . In the
      <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_Prey_(TV_series)" title="Birds of Prey (TV series)">
       <i>
        Birds of Prey
       </i>
       television series
      </a>
      , she was portrayed by actress
      <a href="/wiki/Mia_Sara" title="Mia Sara">
       Mia Sara
      </a>
      (and
      <a href="/wiki/Sherilyn_Fenn" title="Sherilyn Fenn">
       Sherilyn Fenn
      </a>
      in an unaired version of the pilot episode). The character will be making her live-action cinematic debut in the upcoming 2016 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Suicide_Squad_(film)" title="Suicide Squad (film)">
        Suicide Squad
       </a>
      </i>
      portrayed by Australian actress
      <a href="/wiki/Margot_Robbie" title="Margot Robbie">
       Margot Robbie
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">
       IGN
      </a>
      's 2009 list of the Top 100 Comic Book Villains of All Time ranked Harley Quinn as #45.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She was ranked 16th in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Comics_Buyer%27s_Guide" title="Comics Buyer's Guide">
        Comics Buyer's Guide
       </a>
       's
      </i>
      "100 Sexiest Women in Comics" list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

          In other media
         </span>
        </a>
        <ul>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_and_introduction">
       Creation and introduction
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Creation and introduction">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:116px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harley_Quinn_(model_sheet).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="296" data-file-width="114" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b1/Harley_Quinn_%28model_sheet%29.jpg" width="114"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harley_Quinn_(model_sheet).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Harley Quinn, as she appears in the DC Animated Universe.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn first appeared in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_The_Animated_Series" title="Batman: The Animated Series">
        Batman: The Animated Series
       </a>
      </i>
      episode "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joker%27s_Favor" title="Joker's Favor">
       Joker's Favor
      </a>
      ,"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as what was originally supposed to be the animated equivalent of a
      <a href="/wiki/Bit_part" title="Bit part">
       walk-on
      </a>
      role; a number of police officers were to be taken hostage by someone jumping out of a cake, and it was decided that to have the Joker do so himself would be too bizarre (although he ended up doing so anyway). Dini thus created a female sidekick for the Joker.
      <a href="/wiki/Arleen_Sorkin" title="Arleen Sorkin">
       Arleen Sorkin
      </a>
      , a former star of the soap opera
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Days_of_Our_Lives" title="Days of Our Lives">
        Days of Our Lives
       </a>
      </i>
      , appeared in a dream sequence on that series in which she wore a
      <a href="/wiki/Jester" title="Jester">
       jester
      </a>
      costume; Dini used this scene as an inspiration for Quinn.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Having been friends with Sorkin since college, he incorporated aspects of her personality into the character.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 1994
      <a href="/wiki/Graphic_novel" title="Graphic novel">
       graphic novel
      </a>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mad_Love_(comic)" title="Mad Love (comic)">
        Mad Love
       </a>
      </i>
      recounts the character's
      <a href="/wiki/Origin_story" title="Origin story">
       origin
      </a>
      . Told in the style and continuity of
      <i>
       Batman: The Animated Series
      </i>
      and written and drawn by Dini and Timm, the comic book describes
      <b>
       Dr. Harleen Francis Quinzel, M.D.
      </b>
      as an
      <a href="/wiki/Arkham_Asylum" title="Arkham Asylum">
       Arkham Asylum
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">
       psychiatrist
      </a>
      who falls for the Joker and becomes his accomplice and on-off sidekick. The story received wide praise
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and won the
      <a href="/wiki/Eisner_Award" title="Eisner Award">
       Eisner
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Award" title="Harvey Award">
       Harvey Awards
      </a>
      for Best Single Issue Comic of the Year.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_Batman_Adventures" title="The New Batman Adventures">
        The New Batman Adventures
       </a>
      </i>
      series adapted
      <i>
       Mad Love
      </i>
      as the episode of the same name in 1999, making it the second "animated style" comic book adapted for the series. (The other was "Holiday Knights".)
     </p>
     <p>
      She becomes fascinated with the Joker while
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intern" title="Intern">
       interning
      </a>
      at Arkham, and volunteers to analyze him. She falls hopelessly in love nearly instantly with the Joker during their sessions, and she helps him escape from the asylum more than once. When the Joker is returned to Arkham after a battle with Batman, the sight of her badly injured patient drives Harleen insane, leading her to quit her psychiatrist job and don a jester costume to become Harley Quinn, the Joker's sidekick. She later becomes fast friends with
      <a href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy_(comics)" title="Poison Ivy (comics)">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      , who injects her with an
      <a href="/wiki/Antitoxin" title="Antitoxin">
       antitoxin
      </a>
      which gives her super-human strength, agility, and immunity to toxins.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Expanded_role">
       Expanded role
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Expanded role">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      After
      <i>
       Batman: The Animated Series
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_Batman_Adventures" title="The New Batman Adventures">
        The New Batman Adventures
       </a>
      </i>
      , Harley makes several other animated appearances. She appears as one of the four main female characters of the
      <a href="/wiki/Flash_animation" title="Flash animation">
       web cartoon
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gotham_Girls" title="Gotham Girls">
        Gotham Girls
       </a>
      </i>
      . She also made guest appearances in other cartoons in the
      <a href="/wiki/DC_animated_universe" title="DC animated universe">
       DC animated universe
      </a>
      , appearing in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Justice_League_(TV_series)" title="Justice League (TV series)">
        Justice League
       </a>
      </i>
      episode "Wild Cards" (alongside the Joker) and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Static_Shock" title="Static Shock">
        Static Shock
       </a>
      </i>
      episode "Hard as Nails" (alongside
      <a href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy_(comics)" title="Poison Ivy (comics)">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      She appeared in
      <i>
       World's Finest: The Batman/Superman Movie
      </i>
      as a rival and
      <a href="/wiki/Foil_(literature)" title="Foil (literature)">
       foil
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">
       Lex Luthor
      </a>
      's assistant
      <a href="/wiki/Mercy_Graves" title="Mercy Graves">
       Mercy Graves
      </a>
      ; each takes an immediate dislike for the other, at one point fighting brutally with each other as Lex Luthor and the Joker have a business meeting. In the film's
      <a href="/wiki/Climax_(narrative)" title="Climax (narrative)">
       climax
      </a>
      , Harley tied Graves as a
      <a href="/wiki/Human_shield" title="Human shield">
       human shield
      </a>
      to a combat robot set to confront
      <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">
       Superman
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">
       Batman
      </a>
      , but Graves is rescued by the two heroes without suffering any harm (other than the damage Harley had inflicted on her beforehand).
     </p>
     <p>
      The animated movie
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_Beyond:_Return_of_the_Joker" title="Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker">
        Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker
       </a>
      </i>
      takes place in the future, long after the events in
      <i>
       Batman: The Animated Series
      </i>
      . It includes a flashback scene with Harley falling down a deep pit during a battle with Batgirl. At the end of the movie, a pair of twin girls who model themselves on the Joker are released on bail to their grandmother, who angrily berates themto which they answer: "Oh, shut up, Nana Harley!"
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_to_comic_books_and_publication_history">
       Transition to comic books and publication history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Transition to comic books and publication history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HarleyQuinn1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="250" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dd/HarleyQuinn1.jpg/220px-HarleyQuinn1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/dd/HarleyQuinn1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/dd/HarleyQuinn1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HarleyQuinn1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Harley Quinn on the cover of
        <i>
         Harley Quinn
        </i>
        #1 (Dec. 2000). Art by
        <a href="/wiki/Terry_Dodson" title="Terry Dodson">
         Terry Dodson
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After the success of
      <i>
       The Animated Series
      </i>
      , the character proved so popular that she was eventually added to the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_(comic_book)" title="Batman (comic book)">
        Batman
       </a>
      </i>
      comic book
      <a href="/wiki/Canon_(fiction)" title="Canon (fiction)">
       canon
      </a>
      . She first appeared in the original graphic novel,
      <i>
       Batman: Harley Quinn
      </i>
      , as part of the "
      <a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(comics)" title="No Man's Land (comics)">
       No Man's Land
      </a>
      " story, although she had already appeared in the
      <a href="/wiki/Elseworlds" title="Elseworlds">
       Elseworlds
      </a>
      <i>
       Batman: Thrillkiller and Batman: Thrillkiller '62
      </i>
      in 1997. The comic book version of Quinn, like the comic book version of the Joker, is more dangerously violent and less humorously quirky than the animated series version. Despite her noticeably more violent demeanor, Harley does show mercy and compassion from time to time; she notably stops Poison Ivy from killing Batman, instead convincing her to leave the hero hanging bound and gagged from a large statue. Batman is later untied by Batgirl.
     </p>
     <p>
      A
      <i>
       Harley Quinn
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Ongoing_series" title="Ongoing series">
       ongoing series
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was published monthly by
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC Comics
      </a>
      for 38 issues from 2001 to 2003. Creators who contributed to the title included
      <a href="/wiki/Karl_Kesel" title="Karl Kesel">
       Karl Kesel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Terry_Dodson" title="Terry Dodson">
       Terry Dodson
      </a>
      , A.J. Lieberman, and Mike Huddleston. The series dealt with her going solo, eventually starting a gang and then fleeing Gotham for the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(comics)" title="Metropolis (comics)">
       Metropolis
      </a>
      with her friend Poison Ivy. Quinn dies, only to be resurrected and return to Gotham. The series ends with Harley turning herself in to Arkham Asylum, having finally understood that she needs help. We also learn in issue #8 of the comic that Harley had a relationship in college with fellow psychiatry major Guy Kopski whose suicide started her obsession with the Joker. Harley later appears in the
      <a href="/wiki/Jeph_Loeb" title="Jeph Loeb">
       Jeph Loeb
      </a>
      series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Hush" title="Batman: Hush">
        Hush
       </a>
      </i>
      . She is next seen in a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Villains_United" title="Villains United">
        Villains United
       </a>
      </i>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Infinite_Crisis" title="Infinite Crisis">
        Infinite Crisis
       </a>
      </i>
      special, where she is one of the many villains who escape from Arkham (although she is knocked unconscious the moment she escapes).
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/One_Year_Later" title="One Year Later">
        One Year Later
       </a>
      </i>
      continuity, Harley Quinn is an inmate at Arkham, glimpsed briefly in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Detective_Comics" title="Detective Comics">
        Detective Comics
       </a>
      </i>
      #823.
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley next appeared in
      <i>
       Batman
      </i>
      #663, in which she helps the Joker with a plan to kill all his former henchmen, unaware that the "punch line" to the scheme is her own death. Upon realizing this, she shoots him in the shoulder.
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley resurfaces in
      <i>
       Detective Comics
      </i>
      #831, written by Paul Dini. Harley has spent the last year applying for parole, only to see her request systematically rejected by Bruce Wayne, the layman member of Arkham's medical commission. She is kidnapped by Peyton Riley, the new female
      <a href="/wiki/Ventriloquist_(comics)" title="Ventriloquist (comics)">
       Ventriloquist
      </a>
      , who offers her a job; Harley turns the job down out of respect for the memory of Arnold Wesker, the original Ventriloquist, who attempted to cheer her up during her first week in Arkham while the Joker was still on the loose. She then helps Batman and
      <a href="/wiki/James_Gordon_(comics)" title="James Gordon (comics)">
       Commissioner Gordon
      </a>
      foil the impostor's plans. Although Riley escapes, Bruce Wayne is impressed with Harley's effort at redemption, and agrees with granting her parole.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_Prey_(comics)" title="Birds of Prey (comics)">
        Birds of Prey
       </a>
      </i>
      #105, Harley Quinn is revealed as the sixth member of the
      <a href="/wiki/Secret_Six_(comics)" title="Secret Six (comics)">
       Secret Six
      </a>
      . In issue #108, upon hearing that
      <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Gordon" title="Barbara Gordon">
       Oracle
      </a>
      has sent the Russian authorities footage of teammate
      <a href="/wiki/Deadshot" title="Deadshot">
       Deadshot
      </a>
      murdering the Six's employer as payback for double-crossing them, Harley asks, "Is it a bad time to say 'I quit'?", thus leaving the team.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Countdown_(DC_Comics)" title="Countdown (DC Comics)">
        Countdown
       </a>
      </i>
      #43, Harley appears to have reformed and is shown to be residing in an
      <a href="/wiki/Amazons_(DC_Comics)" title="Amazons (DC Comics)">
       Amazon
      </a>
      -run women's shelter. Having abandoned her jester costume and clown make-up, she now only wears an Amazonian
      <a href="/wiki/Stola" title="Stola">
       stola
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Chiton_(costume)" title="Chiton (costume)">
       chiton
      </a>
      . She befriends the former
      <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">
       Catwoman
      </a>
      replacement Holly Robinson, and then succeeds in persuading her to join her at the shelter, where she is working as an assistant. They are both brought to
      <a href="/wiki/Themyscira_(DC_Comics)" title="Themyscira (DC Comics)">
       Themiscyra
      </a>
      by "Athena" (really
      <a href="/wiki/Granny_Goodness" title="Granny Goodness">
       Granny Goodness
      </a>
      ) and begin Amazon training. Holly and Harley then meet the real Athena, and encounter
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Marvel" title="Mary Marvel">
       Mary Marvel
      </a>
      . The group reveal Granny's deception, and Holly, Harley, and Mary follow her as she retreats to
      <a href="/wiki/Apokolips" title="Apokolips">
       Apokolips
      </a>
      . Mary finds the Olympian gods, whom Granny had been holding prisoner, and the group frees them. Harley is granted powers by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thalia_(muse)" title="Thalia (muse)">
       Thalia
      </a>
      as a reward. Upon returning to Earth, the powers vanish, and Harley and Holly return to
      <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">
       Gotham City
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn joins forces with
      <a href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy_(comics)" title="Poison Ivy (comics)">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">
       Catwoman
      </a>
      in the series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City_Sirens" title="Gotham City Sirens">
        Gotham City Sirens
       </a>
      </i>
      . Having moved in with Pamela Isley at the
      <a href="/wiki/Riddler" title="Riddler">
       Riddler
      </a>
      's apartment, she meets up with Catwoman, who offers for the three of them to live and work together. A new villain who tried to take down Selina Kyle named Boneblaster breaks into the apartment, and the three of them have to move after they defeat him. Later, after a chance encounter with
      <a href="/wiki/Hush_(comics)" title="Hush (comics)">
       Hush
      </a>
      , the Joker attempts to kill her, apparently out of jealousy. Quinn is rescued by Ivy and Catwoman, and it is later revealed that her attacker wasn't the real Joker, but one of his old henchmen impersonating him.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City_Sirens" title="Gotham City Sirens">
        Gotham City Sirens
       </a>
      </i>
      #7 establishes that she was born and raised in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bensonhurst" title="Bensonhurst">
       Bensonhurst
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      , into a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
       Jewish
      </a>
      -
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
       Catholic
      </a>
      family. Her father is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Con_artist" title="Con artist">
       con artist
      </a>
      who is still in jail. Her brother, Barry, is a slob with dreams of rock stardom, and her mother, Sharon, wants her to stop the "villain and hero stuff." It is stated that the reason why Harley chose to become a psychologist in the first place was to try and understand her own broken family.
     </p>
     <p>
      On a certain instance Harley attempted to steal from Two-Face and the Riddler, but was caught and they were not happy. Later, Poison Ivy discovers Harley bound and gagged in a closet, and Ivy removes the gag and unties her.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following a number of adventures with Catwoman and Ivy, Harley betrays them and breaks into Arkham with the goal of killing the Joker for abusing her as often as he did. However, Harley ultimately chooses to instead release Joker from his cell, and together the two orchestrate a violent takeover of the facility that results in most of the guards and staff members either being killed or taken hostage by the inmates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Harley and the Joker are eventually defeated by Batman and Catwoman, and Harley is last seen being wheeled away while bound in a straitjacket and muzzle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Shortly after this, Poison Ivy breaks into Harley's cell and attempts to kill her for her betrayal, but instead offers to free her if she helps kill Catwoman, who had left both of her fellow Sirens behind in Arkham. Harley agrees, and the two set out to trap Catwoman.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the ensuing fight, Catwoman says that she saw good in them and only wanted to help. Just as Batman is about to arrest them, Catwoman helps the two of them escape.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_New_52">
       The New 52
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The New 52">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Following DC's
      <a href="/wiki/The_New_52" title="The New 52">
       2011 relaunch
      </a>
      of all its titles, Harley Quinn's costume and appearance is fully revamped. Harley Quinn has a more revealing costume, altered hair color, and bleached skin. Her hair is half-red and half-black, like the jester cap of her previous incarnation, rather than fully blonde. Consistent with her new origin, her bleached skin is the result of being kicked into a vat of acid by the Joker.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HarleyNew52.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="472" data-file-width="356" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/50/HarleyNew52.png/220px-HarleyNew52.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/50/HarleyNew52.png/330px-HarleyNew52.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/50/HarleyNew52.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HarleyNew52.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Harley Quinn as she appears in the New 52 relaunch of DC Comics. Art from
        <i>
         Harley Quinn
        </i>
        vol. 2 #0 (Jan. 2014).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After a falling out with the Joker, she goes into a murderous frenzy, directed towards people responsible for the Joker's imprisonment. Captured by
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Canary" title="Black Canary">
       Black Canary
      </a>
      , she is forcibly inducted into the
      <a href="/wiki/Suicide_Squad" title="Suicide Squad">
       Suicide Squad
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Waller" title="Amanda Waller">
       Amanda Waller
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, when she discovers that the Joker is rumored to be dead, it takes a further toll in her already addled mind, and betraying the Suicide Squad, she puts their safety and secrecy at risk by turning herself into the Gotham Police Department in a plot to gain access to the skinned face of the Joker.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Her plan apparently pays off, and she manages to recover the face, though in a further psychotic episode, Harley captures and ties up Deadshot and places the skinned face of the Joker over Deadshot's face, so that she can carry on a "conversation" with her dead lover. Deadshot lures Harley in close, shooting and severely injuring her during the conversation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the Joker returns to Gotham in the "
      <a href="/wiki/Death_of_the_Family" title="Death of the Family">
       Death of the Family
      </a>
      " storyline, he forces her to disguise herself in his old
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Hood#The_Joker" title="Red Hood">
       Red Hood
      </a>
      costume and trick Batman into coming to the chemical plant where they first met. Batman then falls into a tank and demands Harley to tell him where Joker is. But she only replies, in tears, that he's no longer the Joker she had fallen in love with.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 16, 2013, DC announced that a new
      <i>
       Harley Quinn
      </i>
      ongoing comic book series would begin publication in November 2013, co-written by
      <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Conner" title="Amanda Conner">
       Amanda Conner
      </a>
      and her husband
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Palmiotti" title="Jimmy Palmiotti">
       Jimmy Palmiotti
      </a>
      , cover illustrated by Conner and illustrated by Chad Hardin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The series has notably become distanced from the "Batman Family" of DC publications in both tone and premise, with Harley no longer having any significant connection to either Batman or the Joker following the "Death of the Family" storyline. In the series, Harley Quinn has become a landlady at
      <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">
       Coney Island
      </a>
      , is a part-time member of a roller derby team and has returned to psychiatric work under her real alias, indicating that Harley's real identity is not public knowledge in the new status quo. Under Conner and Palmiotti's writing, Harley has been reinvented as an anti-hero rather than a villain, who values human life and actively tries to improve life in her neighborhood. Between issues #11 and #13 Harley formed a brief partnership with an amnesiac
      <a href="/wiki/Power_Girl" title="Power Girl">
       Power Girl
      </a>
      and battled
      <a href="/wiki/Clock_King" title="Clock King">
       Clock King
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sportsmaster" title="Sportsmaster">
       Sportsmaster
      </a>
      before Power Girl's memory was restored and she left Harley at the top of the
      <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">
       Eiffel Tower
      </a>
      as punishment for her deceit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Harley attempts to coerce a romantic connection with her tenant Mason, but was unable to make the date due to the multitude of responsibilities in her life, balancing her two jobs with her commitment to her roller derby team and her career as a crime-fighter.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With support from her friend
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy" title="Poison Ivy">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      , Harley makes amends with Mason and turns to the internet to recruit other young women in a crime-fighting team she is forming.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Harley Quinn
      </i>
      has featured a few standalone specials which are not directly connected to the main series and feature multiple artists. In the
      <a href="/wiki/Scratch_and_sniff" title="Scratch and sniff">
       scratch and sniff
      </a>
      -themed Annual issue, Harley briefly returned to Gotham to save her friend
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy" title="Poison Ivy">
       Poison Ivy
      </a>
      , as the
      <a href="/wiki/Arkham_Asylum" title="Arkham Asylum">
       Arkham Asylum
      </a>
      employees monitoring her had brainwashed her to create a hallucinogenic pathogen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valentines_Day" title="Valentines Day">
       Valentines Day
      </a>
      Special, Harley returned to Gotham to win a prize date with Bruce Wayne (who unbeknownst to her is Batman) and finds herself fighting animal rights activists-turned-supervillain blackmailers. She shares a brief intimate moment with Bruce Wayne. At Coney Island, Batman informs Harley that while he still distrusts her, he admires her attempt at heroism and promises not to interfere. Harley kisses Batman and tells him to get "lessons" on kissing from Bruce Wayne, to which Batman privately grins.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A spin-off series was launched in June 2015,
      <i>
       Harley Quinn and Power Girl
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Romantic_Relationship_with_Poison_Ivy">
       Romantic Relationship with Poison Ivy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Romantic Relationship with Poison Ivy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      It has been stated by D.C. Comics that Harley and Poison Ivy are in a non-monogamous romantic relationship.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">
       Controversy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Controversy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In September 2013,
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC Comics
      </a>
      announced a contest for fans and artists, "Break into comics with Harley Quinn!",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in which contestants were to draw Harley in four different
      <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">
       suicide
      </a>
      scenarios. This contest drew controversy not only because it was announced close to
      <a href="/wiki/National_Suicide_Prevention_Week" title="National Suicide Prevention Week">
       National Suicide Prevention Week
      </a>
      , but because some artists did not like the sexualized portrayal of Harley in the fourth scenario, in which Harley attempts suicide while naked in her bath tub.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_versions">
       Other versions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other versions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Harley Quinn's first major appearance outside the Batman animated world was in the
       <a href="/wiki/Elseworlds" title="Elseworlds">
        Elseworlds
       </a>
       miniseries
       <i>
        Thrillkiller
       </i>
       . This version of Harley is a schoolgirl named
       <b>
        Hayley Fitzpatrick
       </b>
       who dresses up in order to help a female version of the Joker called Bianca Steeplechase. The relationship between this lesbian or
       <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">
        bisexual
       </a>
       Joker and Harley Quinn is short-lived but noticeably more
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egalitarian" title="Egalitarian">
        egalitarian
       </a>
       than its heterosexual counterpart in mainstream DC continuity. After Batgirl kills Bianca, Harley is shown killing her own family, intent on revenge in the final frames of the story.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         29
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Elseworlds_80-Page_Giant" title="Elseworlds 80-Page Giant">
         Elseworlds 80-Page Giant
        </a>
       </i>
       , one of the stories is about
       <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">
        Lex Luthor
       </a>
       as a music producer. One of his groups is, as the press puts it, "
       <a href="/wiki/Alternative_lifestyle" title="Alternative lifestyle">
        alternative lifestyle
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">
        folkies
       </a>
       Ivy and Harley."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         30
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       On the new
       <a href="/wiki/Earth-Three" title="Earth-Three">
        Earth-3
       </a>
       , Harleen Quinzel is the Jokester's business manager. She is killed by
       <a href="/wiki/Owlman_(comics)" title="Owlman (comics)">
        Owlman
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         31
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Joker_(graphic_novel)" title="Joker (graphic novel)">
        2008 graphic novel
        <i>
         Joker
        </i>
       </a>
       , Harley Quinn appears as the Joker's helper and
       <a href="/wiki/Aide-de-camp" title="Aide-de-camp">
        aide-de-camp
       </a>
       . She at one point acts as a
       <a href="/wiki/Stripper" title="Stripper">
        stripper
       </a>
       (though this may be a ruse), and is never shown speaking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         32
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_(TV_series)#Batman_.2766" title="Batman (TV series)">
        Batman '66
       </a>
       , a version of Harley Quinn appears as Dr. Quinn, a psychiatric specialist at Arkham Asylum here called Arkham
       <i>
        Institute
       </i>
       for the Criminally Insane. She convinces Joker to cooperate with Batman and Robin in exchange for approving his comedy night proposal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         33
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In the alternate timeline of the 2011 "
       <a href="/wiki/Flashpoint_(comics)" title="Flashpoint (comics)">
        Flashpoint
       </a>
       " storyline, an alternate version of the character named
       <b>
        Yo-Yo
       </b>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Martha_Wayne" title="Martha Wayne">
        Joker
       </a>
       's female assistant.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">

        <i>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="In_other_media">
       In other media
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: In other media">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">
       Television
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Television">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="322" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bd/HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg/220px-HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bd/HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bd/HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HarleyBirdsOfPrey.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Mia_Sara" title="Mia Sara">
         Mia Sara
        </a>
        portraying Harley Quinn in
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_Prey_(TV_series)" title="Birds of Prey (TV series)">
          Birds of Prey
         </a>
        </i>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2002, a live-action television series called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_Prey_(TV_series)" title="Birds of Prey (TV series)">
        Birds of Prey
       </a>
      </i>
      , loosely based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_Prey_(comics)" title="Birds of Prey (comics)">
       comic
      </a>
      of the same name, included Harley Quinn as a psychotic psychiatrist and main antagonist. The character was portrayed by actress
      <a href="/wiki/Mia_Sara" title="Mia Sara">
       Mia Sara
      </a>
      (replacing
      <a href="/wiki/Sherilyn_Fenn" title="Sherilyn Fenn">
       Sherilyn Fenn
      </a>
      from an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unaired_Pilot_(Birds_of_Prey)" title="Unaired Pilot (Birds of Prey)">
       unaired pilot episode
      </a>
      ). The show aired only 13 episodes. In this show, she is portrayed as an older, far more calculating and sinister character than her bubbly comic and cartoon personas. Picking up where the Joker had left off, Harleen Quinzel used her day job as a psychiatrist to achieve her savage purpose  to take control of the city of New Gotham. She does not wear a costume, although she does wear an outfit that is reminiscent of her cartoon costume in the series finale "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Eyes" title="Devil's Eyes">
       Devil's Eyes
      </a>
      ." In that episode, she uses experimental technology to transfer
      <a href="/wiki/Metahuman" title="Metahuman">
       metahuman
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Mind_control" title="Mind control">
       mind control
      </a>
      powers to herself. She occasionally makes reference to her "sweet Mr. J.", laments his loss as a Gotham City crime boss and hints at a past relationship reminiscent to that of the animated series. A criminal known as the Crawler addresses her as "the Joker's girlfriend" in the seventh episode "Split."
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn makes an appearance on the
      <a href="/wiki/Kids%27_WB" title="Kids' WB">
       Kids' WB
      </a>
      series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Batman_(TV_series)" title="The Batman (TV series)">
        The Batman
       </a>
      </i>
      , voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Hynden_Walch" title="Hynden Walch">
       Hynden Walch
      </a>
      . In the episode "Two of a Kind" (written by her co-creator Paul Dini), this version of the character is at first the host of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_psychology" title="Pop psychology">
       pop psychology
      </a>
      television show "
      <i>
       Heart To Heart With Harley
      </i>
      ". Harleen Quinzel claims to have obtained a degree in psychology from an
      <a href="/wiki/Online_degree" title="Online degree">
       online educational institution
      </a>
      , and she gives off-the-cuff advice to her callers that usually hurts more than it helps, resulting in a lot of controversy in the media which the
      <a href="/wiki/Joker_(comics)" title="Joker (comics)">
       Joker
      </a>
      finds amusing being a fan of her show. Her boss Jimmy Herbert becomes fed up with her irresponsible behavior and cancels the show on the air after she stages an ambush of Bruce Wayne on her show under a false promise to help promote a charity-drive for crime victims. Joker sees the episode and knows that Harley's having an emotional breakdown, proceeding to take advantage of the situation by making her a partner. Harley rationalizes joining Joker by telling herself that she will be able to get a tell-all that will restore her career, but then she ends up rampaging across Gotham city as Joker's partner-in-crime. Eventually, Harley learns that the network is planning to share with the police a psychological profile of her by TV psychologist Dr. Elliot Blaine, so she plans to destroy the network as revenge for her firing, something which Joker finds amusing. However, she is foiled by Batman,
      <a href="/wiki/Dick_Grayson" title="Dick Grayson">
       Robin
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Gordon" title="Barbara Gordon">
       Batgirl
      </a>
      , and she is arrested after Joker deserts her. She seemingly regrets taking up with Joker. However, once she has been taken into a police car, she sees that Joker has left her an affectionate message, and instantly falls in love again. She has a few short appearances in the episode "Rumor" and a slightly larger appearance in "The Metal Face of Comedy". This incarnation wears a slightly different costume than the one she wears in
      <i>
       Batman: The Animated Series
      </i>
      as in this depiction, the black parts of the original are dark red, the headdress is larger than the original, the inverted diamond pattern on the shoulders and thighs is absent, her gloves are fingerless, and her mask conceals her eyes.
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn appeared in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_The_Brave_and_the_Bold" title="Batman: The Brave and the Bold">
        Batman: The Brave and the Bold
       </a>
      </i>
      , voiced by Meghan Strange. This version is a henchwoman of the Joker modeled after a 1920's
      <a href="/wiki/Flapper" title="Flapper">
       flapper
      </a>
      woman (shown in black-and-white) instead of her traditional costume. In the episode "Legends of the Dark Mite!" while
      <a href="/wiki/Bat-Mite" title="Bat-Mite">
       Bat-Mite
      </a>
      is giving a speech at the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">
       Comic-Con
      </a>
      , there is a brief cameo of
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dini" title="Paul Dini">
       Paul Dini
      </a>
      (Harley Quinn's creator) dressed up as the woman. She appears alongside the Joker in "Emperor Joker!". Though she has a mutual crush on Bat-Mite, she ultimately proves to love Joker more. Alongside virtually every other character that appeared during the show's three season run, Harley makes a cameo appearance in the
      <a href="/wiki/Series_finale" title="Series finale">
       series finale
      </a>
      "Mitefall!" She is shown with Joker at the show's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrap_party" title="Wrap party">
       wrap party
      </a>
      and kicks Gagsworthy when he tries to approach Joker.
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn makes a cameo appearance in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Arrow_(TV_series)" title="Arrow (TV series)">
        Arrow
       </a>
      </i>
      season two episode "Suicide Squad". voiced again by Tara Strong, while physically portrayed (in an obscured fashion) by Cassidy Alexa (credited as "Deranged Squad Female").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The series star
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Amell" title="Stephen Amell">
       Stephen Amell
      </a>
      revealed in an interview that she was originally set to appear in the season two finale episode "Unthinkable," but was cut due to time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The show's producer
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Kreisberg" title="Andrew Kreisberg">
       Andrew Kreisberg
      </a>
      revealed that there were plans for the character to appear, but series actress
      <a href="/wiki/Willa_Holland" title="Willa Holland">
       Willa Holland
      </a>
      revealed that they had been axed due to the Suicide Squad film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">

     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Web_series">
       Web series
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Web series">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Harley Quinn (credited as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_(comics)" title="Harlequin (comics)">
         Harlequin
        </a>
       </i>
       ) appears in the first episode of the web series
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Justice_League:_Gods_and_Monsters_Chronicles" title="Justice League: Gods and Monsters Chronicles">
         Justice League: Gods and Monsters Chronicles
        </a>
       </i>
       where she kidnapped and mutilated an unknown number of people and made toys and dolls out of the bodies. She fights Batman after he frees her latest victim and ends up surrendering, only to be drained of her blood after Batman reveals himself to be a vampire. She is once again voiced by
       <a href="/wiki/Tara_Strong" title="Tara Strong">
        Tara Strong
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Film">
       Film
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Film">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Live-action">
       Live-action
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Live-action">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Prior to the release of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_%26_Robin_(film)" title="Batman &amp; Robin (film)">
        Batman &amp; Robin
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Protosevich" title="Mark Protosevich">
       Mark Protosevich
      </a>
      was commissioned by
      <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">
       Warner Bros.
      </a>
      to write a script for a fifth
      <i>
       Batman
      </i>
      film titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_(1989_film_series)#Canceled_projects" title="Batman (1989 film series)">
        Batman Triumphant
       </a>
      </i>
      to be directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Joel_Schumacher" title="Joel Schumacher">
       Joel Schumacher
      </a>
      , with Harley Quinn and the
      <a href="/wiki/Scarecrow_(DC_Comics)" title="Scarecrow (DC Comics)">
       Scarecrow
      </a>
      as the film's villains. Rumors spread that the character was to be portrayed by
      <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">
       Madonna
      </a>
      . Protosevich wrote her as the Joker's daughter seeking revenge, not his lover and henchgirl. This change was made in order to keep some on-screen continuity with the 1989 film in which Joker was killed by Batman, and rumors also circulated that
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicholson" title="Jack Nicholson">
       Jack Nicholson
      </a>
      might reprise his role in a nightmare sequence caused by Scarecrow's fear toxin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to a lackluster box office run of
      <i>
       Batman and Robin
      </i>
      , bad Internet buzz, and poor critical reception,
      <i>
       Batman Triumphant
      </i>
      was never made, and the film franchise went on hiatus for eight years until
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">
        Batman Begins
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2005.
     </p>
     <p>
      The character will be making her live-action cinematic debut in the upcoming 2016 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Suicide_Squad_(film)" title="Suicide Squad (film)">
        Suicide Squad
       </a>
      </i>
      portrayed by Australian actress
      <a href="/wiki/Margot_Robbie" title="Margot Robbie">
       Margot Robbie
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Animation">
       Animation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley_Quinn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Animation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn appears in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman_Beyond:_Return_of_the_Joker" title="Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker">
        Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker
       </a>
      </i>
      , again voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Arleen_Sorkin" title="Arleen Sorkin">
       Arleen Sorkin
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Justice_League:_Crisis_on_Two_Earths" title="Justice League: Crisis on Two Earths">
        Justice League: Crisis on Two Earths
       </a>
      </i>
      , Harley Quinn is the name of a monkey owned by the Jester (Joker's Parallel Earth equivalent).
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn appears in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Lego_Batman:_The_Movie_%E2%80%93_DC_Super_Heroes_Unite" title="Lego Batman: The Movie  DC Super Heroes Unite">
        Lego Batman: The Movie  DC Super Heroes Unite
       </a>
      </i>
      , an adaptation of the video game of the
      <a href="/wiki/Lego_Batman_2:_DC_Super_Heroes" title="Lego Batman 2: DC Super Heroes">
       same name
      </a>
      , with
      <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bailey_(voice_actress)" title="Laura Bailey (voice actress)">
       Laura Bailey
      </a>
      reprising her role.
     </p>
     <p>
      Yo-Yo appears in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Justice_League:_The_Flashpoint_Paradox" title="Justice League: The Flashpoint Paradox">
        Justice League: The Flashpoint Paradox
       </a>
      </i>
      , again voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Hynden_Walch" title="Hynden Walch">
       Hynden Walch
      </a>
      . In the
      <a href="/wiki/Flashpoint_(comics)" title="Flashpoint (comics)">
       Flashpoint
      </a>
      reality, she is seen fighting
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wayne" title="Thomas Wayne">
       Batman
      </a>
      . After a fight where she uses deadly yo-yos, Batman interogates Yo-Yo for the
      <a href="/wiki/Martha_Wayne" title="Martha Wayne">
       Joker
      </a>
      's location. When she doesn't give an answer, Batman throws her off the building, only for
      <a href="/wiki/Cyborg_(comics)" title="Cyborg (comics)">
       Cyborg
      </a>
      to save her at the last second.
     </p>
     <p>
      Harley Quinn is one of the main characters in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Assault_on_Arkham" title="Batman: Assault on Arkham">
        Batman: Assault on Arkham
       </a>
      </i>
      , again voiced by Hynden Walch. In this version, she is pressganged by
      <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Waller" title="Amanda Waller">
       Amanda Waller
      </a>
      into joining the Suicide Squad, and must venture to Arkham Asylum on a mission to retrieve the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riddler_(comics)" title="Riddler (comics)">
       Riddler
      </a>
      for Waller. Having once worked at the Asylum and knowing its layout and schedules, she is considered vital for the task. Harley seems to be interested in
      <a href="/wiki/Deadshot" title="Deadshot">
       Deadshot
      </a>
      , but ultimately rejoins the Joker and reveals having intended all along to use the mission in order to invade Arkham and break him out. During their escape, Harley battles Batman as Joker faces Deadshot. Both are defeated, but their fates are not revealed. As the film takes place before
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_Asylum" title="Batman: Arkham Asylum">
        Batman: Arkham Asylum
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_City" title="Batman: Arkham City">
        Batman: Arkham City
       </a>
      </i>
      , it is assumed that Harley was recaptured, while Joker escaped.
     </p>

She plays a minor role in T.O.Morrow's hideout, as she has gone there with the Joker to pursue Morrow. Harley is the basic Legends PVP character, granted to Villains without having to spend Marks of Legend. If a player using Harley defeats an enemy player using Joker, the player will get a feat called Mad Love.
